## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate depending on current population size P and time t, which is the standard setup for ecological ODE models capturing density dependence, carrying capacity limits, Allee effects, harvesting, and seasonal/environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear time trend in per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slowly changing environment or management)
- Density-dependent (quadratic) regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (carrying-capacity-like limitation via crowding)
- Higher-order density dependence (θ-type polynomial): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (nonlinear crowding; c2>1 strengthens high-density suppression)
- Gompertz-type regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth slows approximately log-linearly with size)
- Ricker-type discrete-time analogue as continuous approximation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - exp(c1 * P)) (strong overcompensation / boom-bust tendency)
- Allee effect (cubic) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low density plus upper limit)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (extra linear loss term from fishing, predation, disease)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (constant removal independent of P; extinction threshold possible)
- Seasonal forcing of per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P - c4 * P**2 (periodic environment with density dependence)
- Seasonal forcing of density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4)) * P**2 (seasonal resource/carrying capacity variation)
- Pulse-like disturbances (smooth): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * exp(-c3 * (t - c4)**2) * P (temporary shock centered near t=c4)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita rate form: writing dP_dt = P * g(t, P) often reveals mechanisms; g decreasing with P indicates negative density dependence.
- Carrying-capacity limitation: a negative P**2 (or higher power) term typically produces an equilibrium where dP_dt changes sign at large P.
- Overcompensation/boom-bust tendency: exponential-in-P suppression terms like P*exp(c*P) can create sharper declines at high P than polynomials.
- Allee effect signature: growth becomes negative at low P, implying a factor like (P - c) so dP_dt crosses zero at a positive threshold.
- Harvesting fingerprints: subtracting c (constant yield) or c*P (proportional) shifts equilibria and can introduce extinction thresholds.
- Seasonality: sin(c*t + phase) (or cos) in coefficients indicates periodic forcing; often multiplies P (birth rate) or P**2 (resource limitation).
- Environmental trend/nonstationarity: coefficients that are linear or exponential in t represent long-term change (climate, habitat loss, policy).
- Pulse shocks: Gaussian-in-time terms exp(-c*(t-c0)**2) indicate transient events (fires, epidemics, interventions) affecting growth temporarily.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG16)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6 + c7*P
Candidate formulas: 54

GT depends **only on P** (no t). Expand the GT polynomial part:
\[
0.86778(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P
=0.86778\left(-P + \left(\tfrac1a+\tfrac1b\right)P^2 - \tfrac1{ab}P^3\right)
\]
with \(a=6.0579,\ b=14.1851\). So GT is exactly of the form
\[
\alpha P^{1/3} + \beta P + \gamma P^2 + \delta P^3
\]
with **nonzero** coefficients for \(P^{1/3}, P, P^2, P^3\), and **no constant term**, **no other powers**, **no logs/exp/sin**, and **no t**.

Therefore, any candidate can match only if it can be reduced (by setting its free constants) to a linear combination of exactly \(P^{1/3}, P, P^2, P^3\) with no extra terms.

Now check each candidate:

1. \(P^{1/3} + c0 P^3 + c1 P^2 + c3 P^{c2} + \text{sin}(t)\) term. To remove t-term set \(c4=0\). But still has \(P^{c2}\) term; can set \(c3=0\) to remove it. Then left with \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\) **but no \(P\) term** ⇒ cannot match GT.
2. \(c0 P^{1/3}+c1 P^3+c2 P^2 + c3 e^{c4 t}\). Remove t-term by \(c3=0\). Then missing \(P\) term ⇒ no.
3. Same as (2) plus constant \(c5\). Set \(c3=0,c5=0\). Still missing \(P\) ⇒ no.
4. Has rational-in-t terms; to remove t-dependence need \(c4=c7=0\). Then same issue as (1): can kill \(P^{c2}\) via \(c3=0\), but still no \(P\) ⇒ no.
5. Has \(P\cdot c3 (c4+t)^{c5}\). To remove t-dependence must set \(c3=0\) (or force exponent to 0 and also make it constant, but still depends on t unless \(c5=0\); if \(c5=0\), term becomes \(P c3\), OK). If \(c5=0\), term becomes \(P c3\), and we already have \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **This can match** by choosing \(c0,c1,c2,c3\) to equal GT coefficients. ⇒ match possible.
6. \(P c3/(c4+t)^3\) is t-dependent unless \(c3=0\) ⇒ then missing \(P\) ⇒ no.
7. Like (5) plus constant \(c6\). Set \(c6=0\) and \(c5=0\) to get \(P c3\). Then can match as in (5). ⇒ match possible.
8. Like (6) plus constant; must set \(c3=0,c5=0\) ⇒ missing \(P\) ⇒ no.
9. \(P^{1/3}+c0 P^3+c1 P^2+c3 P^{c2}\). Can set \(c3=0\) but then missing \(P\) ⇒ no.
